I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Error message for using the record spread syntax with positional-only records is unclear
Looks like an unintentional limitation of compiler (gleam 1.13.0/erlang 27.0).
Unpacking a record with only positional fields results in compilation failure "This is not a record constructor". This is only an issue for unlabelled records.

```gleam
// does not compile
type Positional{
    Positional(Int, Int)
}

pub fn pos_test(){
  let t1 = Positional(1,2)
  let t2 = Positional(..t1) // "This is not a record constructor"
  assert t1 == t2
}
```
`compiler-core/src/type_/expression.rs::3418..3432` returns `Error::RecordUpdateInvalidConstructor` since all-unlabelled record is missing `field_map`

Checking how it's related to #5195 

</pr_description>

  3333	        &mut self,
  3334	        constructor: &TypedExpr,
  3335	        value_constructor: &'c ValueConstructor,
  3336	        record: &TypedExpr,
  3337	    ) -> Result<RecordUpdateVariant<'c>, Error> {
  3338	        let record_type = record.type_();
  3339	        // The record constructor needs to be a function.
  3340	        let (arguments_types, return_type) = match constructor.type_().as_ref() {
  3341	            Type::Fn { arguments, return_ } => (arguments.clone(), return_.clone()),
  3342	            Type::Named { .. } | Type::Var { .. } | Type::Tuple { .. } => {

  3344	                    location: constructor.location(),
  3345	                });
  3346	            }
  3347	        };

  3352	                field_map: Some(field_map),
  3353	                variants_count,
  3354	                variant_index,
  3355	                name,

  3357	            } => (field_map, *variants_count, *variant_index, name.clone()),
  3358	            ValueConstructorVariant::Record {
  3359	                field_map: None, ..
  3360	            } => {
  3361	                return Err(Error::RecordUpdateInvalidConstructor {
  3362	                    location: constructor.location(),
  3363	                });
  3364	            }

  3369	                    location: constructor.location(),
  3370	                });
  3371	            }
  3372	        };

  3375	        // not some unrelated other type. This should not affect our returned type, so we
  3376	        // instantiate a new copy of the generic return type for our value constructor.

  3381	                    location: constructor.location(),
  3382	                });
  3383	            }

Now I understand the full picture. The `Record` variant has `field_map: Option<FieldMap>` where `None` means there are no labelled fields. The `arity` field tells us how many total fields there are.

Now, the fix should be in `infer_record_update_variant`. For a record with `field_map: None`:
- If `variants_count == 1`, we can safely allow the update with an empty `FieldMap`
- If `variants_count > 1`, we should still error (or maybe allow if variant inference works?)

Wait, actually, let me think about this more carefully. For a record with only positional fields:
- If it has only one variant, the spread is always safe (line 3390-3397 already handles this, but we don't reach it because we error out at line 3358-3363 first)
- If it has multiple variants, we could still allow it if we know the variant being spread matches

So the fix should be: instead of returning `RecordUpdateInvalidConstructor` when `field_map` is `None`, we should create an empty `FieldMap` with the correct `arity` (from the record constructor's `arity` field) and continue with the normal flow.

Now I need to understand: for a record with `field_map: None`, we need an empty `FieldMap` with the correct `arity`. But `arity` is available on the `Record` variant. 

However, the `field_map` returned is a reference to the `FieldMap` inside the `value_constructor`. If we have `None`, we can't get a reference to a `FieldMap`. We need to create an empty one.

Looking at `RecordUpdateVariant`:
```rust
struct RecordUpdateVariant<'a> {
    arguments: Vec<Arc<Type>>,
    return_type: Arc<Type>,
    field_map: &'a FieldMap,
}
```

It takes a reference to `FieldMap`. So we'd need a `FieldMap` to exist somewhere. One option is to change `field_map` to `Option<&'a FieldMap>` or to `Cow<'a, FieldMap>`. But that might be a bigger change.

Alternatively, we could create an empty `FieldMap` with the right arity and store it somewhere. But since `RecordUpdateVariant` borrows it, we'd need the `FieldMap` to live long enough.

Let me look at how `field_map` is used in `RecordUpdateVariant`:

1. `has_field` - checks if a label exists in the field map
2. `field_names` - returns the keys of the field map
3. `args_type` - doesn't use field_map directly
4. In `infer_record_update_arguments`:
   - `let mut fields = variant.field_map.fields.clone();` (line 3110)
   - `variant.field_map.indices_to_labels()` (line 3184)
   - `variant.field_map.arity` (line 3187)

For an empty `FieldMap`, `fields` would be empty, `indices_to_labels()` would return empty, and `arity` would be the number of positional fields. This should work correctly - the implicit arguments would all be positional (the `else` branch at line 3215).

So the simplest approach would be to change `RecordUpdateVariant.field_map` from `&'a FieldMap` to `Option<&'a FieldMap>` or to `Cow<'a, FieldMap>`. But let me check if there's a simpler approach.

Actually, looking more carefully, the `RecordUpdateVariant` is created and used within the same function (`infer_record_update`). Let me look at the broader function

```rust
    return_type: Arc<Type>,

}
```

This would require cloning the `FieldMap` in the `Some` case, which is a small cost. Let me check if `FieldMap` is `Clone`:

Line 10: `#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]`

Yes, it derives `Clone`. So we can clone it. And for the `None` case, we create a new `FieldMap::new(arity)`.

Let me check the `Record` variant's `arity` field type: it's `u16`. `FieldMap::arity` is `u32`. And `FieldMap::new(arity: u32)`.

Actually, I think the issue is that the type of an arity-0 constructor like `Empty` is just the return type (e.g., `Type::Named { name: "Empty", ... }`), not `Type::Fn`. For arity > 0, it's `Type::Fn { args: [...], return_: ... }`.

So at line 3340-3346, when `constructor.type_()` is `Type::Named` (for an arity-0 constructor), it hits the error case and returns `RecordUpdateInvalidConstructor`.

2026-05-30 18:30:35,156 - INFO - swea-agent-gleam-lang__gleam-5482 - 💭 THOUGHT
For the constant case, the `field_map` is used for:
1. `field_map.fields` - to track which labelled fields have been updated
2. Checking for duplicate/unknown fields

For a positional-only record, `field_map.fields` would be empty, which means:
- `implicit_labelled_arguments` would be empty
- `field_map.fields.contains_key(label)` would always be false
- `field_map.fields.keys()` would be empty

So an empty `FieldMap` would work correctly for positional-only records in the constant case too.

Let me fix the constant case as well:

                            location: constructor_location,
                        });
                        return self.new_invalid_constant(location);
                    }

                    ValueConstructorVariant::ModuleFn { .. }
                    | ValueConstructorVariant::LocalVariable { .. } => {
                        self.problems
                            .error(Error::NonLocalClauseGuardVariable { location, name });
                        return self.new_invalid_constant(location);
                    }

                    ValueConstructorVariant::ModuleConstant { literal, .. } => {
                        return literal.clone();
                    }
                };'
